## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and/or external driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Coupled position-velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (position-velocity coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use when oscillation is symmetric
- Even-power terms in x (x²) break spatial symmetry — use when the potential is asymmetric
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - x²)*v or x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- sin(c*x) restoring force indicates a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum) rather than polynomial approximation
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (not t), the system is autonomous and energy-based analysis applies
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicates hardening/softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests conservative or autonomously damped system — look for x and v terms only
- Products v*x^n suggest coupling between kinetic and potential degrees of freedom, common in nonlinear friction models
